Denial of Offer After Acknowledgment Does Not Nullify It
Ruling on denial of offer after acknowledgment with citation from Tatarkhaniyya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that denial of an offer after acknowledgment does not nullify it, and apply it to sale and marriage contracts.

Core Idea
Acknowledgment of an offer, once made, is not undone by subsequent denial.

This lesson examines a specific rule in Hanafi contract law: when a seller claims to have made an offer and the buyer denies it, but later admits to the purchase, the sale is still valid. The source text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq states this clearly, citing al-Tatarkhaniyya. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the weight of acknowledgment (iqrar) in contractual dealings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The core question: does denial of an offer after a party has already acknowledged it nullify the offer?
2
State the ruling from the matn
The text states: 'وإنكار الإيجاب بعد الإقرار به لا يبطله' — denial after acknowledgment does not nullify.
This is the primary ruling.
3
Examine the example
A man says 'I sold you this slave for a thousand' and the buyer initially denies, but later acknowledges the purchase, even after parting. The sale is valid.
The acknowledgment can occur even after the session ends.
4
Extend to marriage contracts
The same rule applies to marriage (nikaah): denial after acknowledgment does not nullify, and later acknowledgment is valid.
The text says 'وكذا النكاح'.
5
Note the commentator's caution
The commentator ends with 'فليتأمل' (let it be considered), suggesting nuance or a possible differing view that requires careful thought.
This caution does not overturn the ruling but invites further scrutiny.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح الإيجاب بقوله رضيت وإنكار الإيجاب بعد الإقرار به لا يبطله حتى لو أقر به بعدما افترقا جاز، وكذا النكاح. قوله : (وإنكار الإيجاب بعد الإقرار به لا يبطله الخ) الذي رأيته في التتارخانية هكذا : رجل قال لآخر كنت بعت منك هذا العبد بألف درهم وقال الآخر لم أشتره منك فسكت البائع حتى قال المشتري في المجلس أو بعدما افترقا قد اشتريت بألف منك جاز وكذا النكاح اهـ. فليتأمل.
And the offer is valid by his saying 'I am satisfied.' And denial of the offer after acknowledging it does not nullify it. Even if he acknowledges it after they have parted, it is valid, and likewise marriage. His statement: (And denial of the offer after acknowledging it does not nullify it, etc.) What I saw in al-Tatarkhaniyya is as follows: A man said to another, 'I sold you this slave for a thousand dirhams,' and the other said, 'I did not buy it from you,' and the seller remained silent until the buyer said, in the session or after they parted, 'I have bought it for a thousand from you,' it is valid, and likewise marriage. End. So let it be considered.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn: if a seller claims he made an offer and the buyer denies it, but later acknowledges the purchase, that acknowledgment is valid and the sale is concluded, even if the acknowledgment occurs after they have left the session. The same applies to marriage contracts. The commentator cites al-Tatarkhaniyya to confirm this ruling, but adds 'فليتأمل' (let it be considered), suggesting there may be a nuance or a differing view that requires careful thought, though he does not elaborate here.

Key Terms
إيجاب (ijab): The offer made in a contract; the seller's statement initiating the sale.
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession; here it refers to the buyer's admission of having made a purchase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a seller says 'I sold you this slave for a thousand' and the buyer initially denies it, then later acknowledges the purchase after they have parted, what is the ruling?
A) The sale is invalid because of the initial denial.
B) The sale is valid because the later acknowledgment is effective.
C) The sale is valid only if the acknowledgment occurs in the same session.
D) The sale is invalid unless the seller repeats the offer.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a buyer's later acknowledgment of a sale cures any prior denial, and the contract is valid even after the parties have separated.

Combined Contracts: Sale and Marriage in One Offer
Ruling on combined offer and acceptance scenarios for sale and marriage (and sale and lease).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a combined offer of sale and marriage and apply it to determine validity when acceptance is partial.

Core Idea
A combined offer of sale and marriage is valid only if both accepted; sale alone invalid, marriage alone valid with portion of customary dowry.

This passage from the matn addresses a nuanced situation in transactional law: a single offer that proposes two different contracts—sale and marriage—for one lump sum. The ruling hinges on whether the offeree accepts both, only the sale, or only the marriage. Understanding this distinction is essential for proper contract formation in Hanafi fiqh, as the legal nature of each contract affects the allocation of the price.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contracts combined
Recognize that the offer contains two distinct contracts: a sale (of an item) and a marriage (of a woman). The lump sum is intended for both.
2
Analyze acceptance of both contracts
If both are accepted, the combined contract is valid. The lump sum is apportioned: the sale portion equals the market value of the item; the marriage portion equals the customary dowry (mahr mithl) of the woman.
3
Examine acceptance of sale alone
If only the sale is accepted, the contract is invalid (lā yajūz). The reason is that the price for the sale is tied to the marriage, so accepting only one leaves the price unspecified.
4
Examine acceptance of marriage alone
If only the marriage is accepted, the marriage is valid, and the husband must pay the portion of the lump sum that equals a proper mahr (mahr mithl). This is because marriage can be valid with a customary dowry even if the exact amount is not fixed.
5
Extend to other combined contracts (sale and lease)
The same principle applies when the offer combines a sale and a lease: a single acceptance covers both, and the lump sum is divided between value and fair rent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا أوجب في عقدين كبعتك هذا وزوجتك هذه بألف فقبلهما جاز وانقسم الألف على مهر مثل هذه وقيمة هذه وإن قبل البيع وحده لا يجوز، وإن قبل النكاح وحده جاز بحصة مهر مثلها من الألف ولو قال بعتك هذه الدار وأجرتك هذه الأرض فقال قبلت يكون جواباً لهما.
And if he makes an offer in two contracts, such as 'I sell you this and I marry you to this [woman] for one thousand,' and he accepts both, it is valid, and the thousand is divided between the mahr of her like and the value of this [item]. If he accepts the sale alone, it is not valid. If he accepts the marriage alone, it is valid with the portion of the mahr of her like from the thousand. And if he said, 'I sell you this house and I rent you this land,' and he said 'I accept,' it is a response to both.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage from the matn addresses the situation where a single offer combines two different contracts: a sale and a marriage (or a sale and a lease). The key ruling is that if the offeree accepts both, the contract is valid and the lump sum is allocated between the two based on the proper value of each: the market value of the sold item and the appropriate mahr for the woman. However, if he accepts only the sale part, it is invalid because the offer was indivisible. If he accepts only the marriage, it is valid, and he owes the portion of the sum that corresponds to a proper mahr. The same principle applies to combining sale and lease: one acceptance covers both.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr mithl): The customary dowry for a woman of similar status; used to determine the portion of the lump sum allocated to marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person says 'I sell you this slave and I marry you to my daughter for one thousand dirhams,' and the offeree accepts only the marriage, what is the ruling?
A) The marriage is invalid because the offer was for both.
B) The marriage is valid and the husband must pay the full thousand.
C) The marriage is valid and the husband pays the portion equal to a proper mahr.
D) The marriage is valid only if the sale is also accepted.

Key Takeaway
A combined offer of sale and marriage is valid only when both are accepted, but acceptance of only the marriage is valid with a customary dowry portion, while acceptance of only the sale is invalid.

Sale Through a Messenger: Acceptance Must Be in the Session
Rulings on sale offers sent via messenger

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a sale offer sent via messenger and explain why acceptance must occur in the same session as the offer.

Core Idea
A sale via messenger requires acceptance in the same session; the messenger merely conveys, not acts.

In Hanafi fiqh, the continuity of offer and acceptance in the same session is essential for most contracts of exchange. When a sale offer is sent via a messenger (rasul), the question arises: does the session of the messenger count as the session of the buyer? This lesson clarifies the ruling, including the distinction between a messenger and an agent, and the special consensus for khul' and manumission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the specific scenario: seller sends an offer through a messenger; buyer accepts after the messenger delivers. State the Hanafi ruling (invalid unless acceptance occurs in the same session as delivery).
The text begins with 'ولو قال بعت هذا العبد فلاناً فبلغه الرسول فقال اشتريت لا يصح' – the basic ruling is that it is not valid.
2
Understand the role of the messenger
Recognize that the messenger (rasul) is a pure conveyor; his words are attributed to the principal (seller). The session for acceptance is the buyer's own session, not the messenger's.
Al-Sighnaqi's restriction (قيده السغناقي في المجلس) emphasizes that acceptance must be in the session where the buyer personally accepts.
3
Distinguish message from agency
If the buyer instructs a third person to say 'I bought' as a message, the sale is valid; if as an agent (وكالة), it is not. The agent's own statement binds the buyer, but the session condition applies differently.
The text: 'إن أخرجه مخرج الرسالة صح وإن أخرجه مخرج الوكالة لا يصح'.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some transmissions in al-Tatarkhaniyya seem to allow acceptance after the session, citing 'the messenger's statement is like the principal's.' The commentator resolves this by attributing rulings to different source books.
Al-Khulasa harmonizes: if the messenger explicitly says 'the seller says: I sold to so-and-so,' acceptance is valid; otherwise not.
5
Apply the special consensus for khul' and manumission
For khul' (divorce by compensation) and manumission for payment, the second part of the contract (acceptance) can occur after the session by consensus. This is an exception to the general rule.
The text: 'فإنه يتوقف شطر العقد من الزوج والمولى على قبول الآخر وراء المجلس بالإجماع'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال بعت هذا العبد فلاناً فبلغه الرسول فقال اشتريت لا يصح، وقيده السغناقي في المجلس. ويصح الرجوع عن الرسالة قبل التبليغ إلا في رواية ولو قال بعت منه فبلغه يا فلان فبلغه غيره جاز وهذا مما يحفظ جداً، ولو قال بعته من فلان الرسول فقال المشتري اشتريته لا يصح. ولو قال بعته من فلان الغائب لم يجز إلا إذا قبل منه فضولي أو يقول بلغه ولو أوجب البيع فقال المخاطب لآخر قل اشتريت فقال الآخر اشتريت إن أخرجه مخرج الرسالة صح وإن أخرجه مخرج الوكالة لا يصح . وكذا الجواب في الإجارة والهبة والكتابة فأما الخلع والعتق على مال فإنه يتوقف شطر العقد من الزوج والمولى على قبول الآخر وراء المجلس بالإجماع. قوله : ( وقيده السغناقي في المجلس كذا في التتارخانية ولم يظهر وجهه فتأمل. قوله: (ولو قال بعته من فلان الرسول) كذا في النسخ وفيه سقط. وعبارة التتارخانية: ولو قال بعته من فلان فبلغه فبلغه الرسول فقال المشتري اشتريت لا يصح انتهت. وقوله «لا يصح مخالف لقوله قبله جاز لكن صاحب التتارخانية عز الحكمين إلى كتابين لا كما فعل المؤلف من تركه العزو وعبارة الخلاصة : رجل قال لآخر بعت هذا العبد من فلان فبلغه فبلغه الرسول فقال اشتريت جاز لأن قول الرسول كقول المرسل، ولو لم يقل بلغه فبلغه وقال المشتري اشتريت لا يصح اهـ.
And if he said, 'I sold this slave to so-and-so,' and the messenger reached him and he said 'I bought,' it is not valid; and al-Sighnaqi restricted it to the session. Revocation of the message before delivery is valid except in one narration. And if he said, 'I sold from him,' and it reached him, 'O so-and-so,' and someone else conveyed it, it is valid, and this is to be memorized well. And if he said, 'I sold it to so-and-so as a messenger,' and the buyer said 'I bought it,' it is not valid. And if he said, 'I sold it to so-and-so who is absent,' it is not valid unless a stranger accepts on his behalf or he says 'it reached him.' And if he made the offer of sale and the addressee said to another, 'Say: I bought,' and the other said 'I bought,' if he intended it as a message, it is valid; if as agency, it is not valid. The same answer applies to lease, gift, and kitaba. As for khul' and manumission for compensation, half of the contract from the husband or master depends on the acceptance of the other even outside the session by consensus. His statement: (And al-Sighnaqi restricted it to the session, as in al-Tatarkhaniyya, and its reason is not apparent, so consider.) His statement: (And if he said, 'I sold it to so-and-so as a messenger'), in the copies it is like that, and there is an omission. The expression of al-Tatarkhaniyya is: 'And if he said, 'I sold it to so-and-so,' and it reached him, and the messenger reached him, and the buyer said 'I bought,' it is not valid.' End. And his statement 'it is not valid' contradicts his earlier 'valid,' but the author of al-Tatarkhaniyya attributed the two rulings to two books, not as the author did by leaving out the attribution. And the expression of al-Khulasa: 'A man said to another, 'I sold this slave to so-and-so,' and it reached him, and the messenger reached him, and he said 'I bought,' it is valid because the statement of the messenger is like the statement of the principal; and if he did not say 'it reached him' and said 'it reached him' and the buyer said 'I bought,' it is not valid. End.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage deals with the intricacies of sale through a messenger. The main ruling states that if a seller sends a message offering a sale, and the messenger delivers it, the buyer's acceptance in the same session is required for validity. If the buyer accepts after the session, it is invalid. The seller may revoke the message before it is delivered. The commentator notes a discrepancy in al-Tatarkhaniyya regarding the validity when the buyer says 'I bought' after receiving the message; one ruling says valid, another invalid. He attributes this to different source books and quotes al-Khulasa which harmonizes: if the messenger says 'the seller says: I sold to so-and-so' then acceptance is valid; if the buyer merely says 'I bought' without the messenger explicitly relaying, it is not valid. Additionally, if the buyer instructs someone else to speak the acceptance, it must be as a message (the second person is merely conveying) not as an agent (where the second person acts for the buyer), otherwise invalid. Special rules apply to khul' and manumission for compensation, where acceptance outside the session is allowed by consensus.

Key Terms
رسول (rasul): A messenger who conveys an offer from the seller to the buyer; his speech is attributed to the principal.
وكالة (wakalah): Agency; in this context, if the second person is made an agent to accept the offer, the ruling differs from mere message.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a seller sends a messenger to a buyer saying 'I sold you this item for a hundred,' and the buyer responds after the session, the sale is:
A) Valid because the messenger's delivery constitutes the session.
B) Invalid because acceptance must be in the same session as the offer.
C) Valid only if the seller had not revoked the message.
D) Valid if the buyer says 'I bought' immediately upon receiving the message.

Key Takeaway
For a sale via messenger, acceptance must occur in the same session as the offer; otherwise the contract is invalid, with the exception of khul' and manumission for compensation.

Conditions for Valid Acceptance (Qabul) in Sales
Commentary on conditions for acceptance in sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid acceptance in a Hanafi sale contract and apply them to determine the validity of a sale in given scenarios.

Core Idea
Acceptance must match the offer in session, scope, and timing; otherwise the sale is invalid.

This lesson examines the detailed conditions for acceptance (qabul) in a sale contract as elaborated in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The Hanafi school places precise requirements on acceptance to ensure mutual consent and avoid uncertainty. We will explore when the word 'na'am' suffices, how prices are determined through conduct, the necessity of session continuity, the prohibition of partial acceptance in unitary transactions, and the effects of revocation, death, or change in the sold item. Understanding these conditions is essential for anyone involved in Islamic commercial transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Acceptance (qabul) in a sale. The overall ruling is that acceptance, when conditions are met, renders the sale valid (sahih). The passage details conditions without which acceptance is invalid.
2
Locate the conditions
The passage discusses multiple conditions: (a) acceptance must be in the same session as the offer; (b) acceptance must cover the entire offer (no partial acceptance in a unitary transaction); (c) acceptance must occur before a change in the sold item; (d) acceptance must occur before revocation by the offeror; (e) the offeror must be alive at the time of acceptance; (f) acceptance can be by word or conduct, even a simple 'na'am' after a question, but sometimes payment is required as confirmation.
These conditions are derived from the scenarios and rulings mentioned in the text.
3
Evaluate the conduct-based price determination
The text presents scenarios from al-Khaniyyah where the last utterance or conduct of the parties determines the price. Understand the principle: when parties bargain and one takes possession without explicit agreement, the last stated price by the party controlling the item governs, provided there is no explicit rejection.
For example, if the item is in the buyer's hand, the seller's last price applies; if in the seller's hand, the buyer's last offer applies.
4
Analyze the partial acceptance rule
For a unitary transaction (safqah wahidah), partial acceptance is invalid because it splits the transaction, introducing a defect of partnership. The passage explains three situations: single offeror with multiple addressees, multiple offerors with single addressee, and single offeror with single addressee. In all cases, division is invalid.
Exception: if the other party consents after partial acceptance and the item can be divided by apportionment, then the partial acceptance becomes a new offer.
5
Understand the simultaneous offer-acceptance dispute
The text notes a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school: some say simultaneous utterances create a valid sale, but others argue that 'simultaneous' really means 'immediately consecutive' because true simultaneity would prevent a valid contract, analogous to salam.
The relied-upon view according to al-Tatar Khaniyyah is that simultaneous is valid, but al-Qahistani disagrees.

Source Text

الثمن لأن النقد دليل التحقيق. وفي الخانية : لو قال أبيعه بخمسة عشر فقال لا آخذه إلا بعشرة فذهب به ولم يقل البائع شيئاً فهو بخمسة عشر إن كان المبيع في يد المشتري حين ساومه وإن كان في يد البائع فأخذه لما بين الثمن توقف البيع على إجازة المشتري الأول ألا أن المشتري لو استهلكه بعد العلم بالثمن كان عليه الثمن، ولو استهلكه قبل العلم بالثمن كان عليه تری٤٤٨كتاب البيعالبيع كما ورجوع الموجب معاً كان الرجوع أولى كما في الخانية، ولو صدر الإيجاب والقبول معاً صح في التتارخانية. ولا يشترط أن يشتمل القبول على الخطاب بعدما صدر الإيجاب بالخطاب فلو قال بعد قوله بعتك اشتريت ولم يقل منك صح كما في فتح القدير. ولو قال بعتكه بألف فقال اشتريته بألف إلى سنة أو بشرط الخيار لم يتم إلا إذا رضي في المجلس؛ كذا في المجتبى. ولا بد من كون القبول قبل تغير المبيع وعليه تفرع ما في الخانية : لو قطعت يد الجارية بعد الإيجاب وأخذ البائع أرشها أو ولدت الجارية أو تخمر العصير ثم صار خلاً لم يصح قبول المشتري .اهـ. وكذا لو كان المبيع عبدين فقتل أحدهما خطأ وأخذ البائع الأرش لم يجز القبول؛ كذا في الظهيرية ولا بد أن يكون قبل رد المخاطب الإيجاب، فلو قال بعتك بألف فقال لا أقبل بل أعطيته بخمسمائة ثم قال أخذته بألف قال أبو يوسف : إن دفعه إليه فهو رضا وإلا فلا كذا في الخانية. وقدمنا في بيان الشرائط أنه لا بد أن يكون القبول في جميع ما أوجب بجميع ما أوجبه فلم يصح القبول في البعض أو بالبعض حيث كانت الصفقة متحدة للزوم تفريق الصفقة المقتضي لعيب الشركة لا من جهة جريان العادة بضم الجيد إلى الرديء ليروج كما وقع في بعض الكتب فإنه لا يشمل ما إذا كان المبيع واحداً فقبل في فة ما البعض كما في الغاية ولا بد من معرف يوجب اتحادها وتفريقها. وحاصل ما ذكروه أن الموجب إذا اتحد وتعدد المخاطب لم يجز التفريق بقبول أحدهما، بائعاً كان الموجب أو مشترياً، وعلى عكسه لم يجز القبول في حصة أحدهما، وإن اتحدا لم يصح قبول المخاطب في البعض فلم يصح تفريقها مطلقاً في الأحوال الثلاثة أعني ما إذا اتحد الموجب أو تعدد أو اتحد القابل أو تعدد لاتحاد الصفقة في الكل، وكذا إذا اتحد العاقدان وتعدد المبيع كأن يوجب في مثليين أو قيمي ومثلي لم يجز تفريقها بالقبول في أحدهما إلا أن يرضى الآخر بذلك بعد قبوله في البعض، ويكون المبيع مما ينقسم الثمن عليه بالإجزاء كعبد واحد أو مكيل أو موزون فيكون القبول إيجاباً والرضا قبولاً وبطل الإيجاب الأول، فإن كان مما لا ينقسم إلا بالقيمة كثوبين قيمته اهـ فليتأمل. ثم ظهر الجواب بأن هذا بعد الإيجاب والقبول من المشتري وقبل العلم بالثمن، وما نحن فيه قبل القبول .اهـ. قوله : (ولو صدر الإيجاب والقبول معاً صح البيع) عزاه في التتارخانية إلى الخلاصة قال : هكذا كان يقول والدي لكن في القهستاني وينبغي أن تكون الواو في قوله «بإيجاب وقبول» بمعنى الفاء فإنهما لو كانا معاً لم ينعقد كما قالوا في السلم .اهـ. وظاهره أنه قاس البيع على السلم وقد صرح في التجنيس بخصوص مسألتنا فقال : رجل قال لآخر بعتك هذا العبد بألف درهم فقال الآخر قبلت وقال البائع رجعت وخرج الكلامان منهما معاً لم يصح البيع لأنه قارن القبول ما يمنع صحة القبول وهو رجوع البائع .اهـ. قوله : (وأخذ البائع أرشها قال في النهر : الظاهر أن التقييد بأخذ الأرش اتفاقي .اهـ. قلت يؤيده ما في التتارخانية عن الظهيرية حيث قال: ودفع أرش اليد إلى البائع أو لم يدفع قوله : (بل) أعطيته بخمسمائة بحذف همزة الاستفهام وفتح تاء المخاطب .
The book of sales. 'I bought this slave of yours for one thousand' and the other said 'yes', the sale is valid because it is a response. And its verification is in what we wrote in al-Qawa'id al-Fiqhiyyah. And it is mentioned in al-Qunyah that 'yes' after the question 'Did you sell to me for such?' or 'Did you buy from me for such?' is a sale if the price is paid, because payment is evidence of confirmation. And in al-Khaniyyah: If he said 'I sell it for fifteen' and [the other] said 'I will not take it except for ten', and he took it and the seller said nothing, then it is for fifteen if the sold item was in the buyer's hand when he bargained; and if it was in the seller's hand and the buyer took it and the seller did not prevent him, then it is for ten. And if it was with the buyer and the buyer said 'I will not take it except for ten' and the seller said 'I will not sell it except for fifteen', then the buyer returned it to him, then took it from the seller's hand and the seller handed it over without saying anything, and the buyer took it, then it is for ten. And if he took a garment from a man and the seller said 'it is for twenty' and the buyer said 'I will not increase you beyond ten', and he took it and went away and it was lost with him, Abu Yusuf said: It is for twenty. And if he took a garment on negotiation and the seller handed it over while negotiating and the seller said 'it is for ten', then it is at the price the seller said. End quote. And in al-Mujtaba: If they proceed with the contract after differing in their statements, consideration is given to the last of their words, and judgment is based on that. End quote. And acceptance must be in the session of offer; if one of them stands before it, it is invalid; and it is said [he may remain] as long as he is in his place. And if the seller speaks to a person about his need, then it is invalidated. And in al-Mujtaba: If the buyer offers 'for you' or 'your slave', it is a sale. And the offeror must be alive until acceptance; if he dies it is invalid, except for a case mentioned by Qadi Khan in his Fatawa: If he bequeaths the sale of his house to a man and says 'my house is sold to him for one thousand after his death', it is valid; likewise Abu Yusuf mentioned it in al-Nawadir. And there must be [mention of] dirham? And he died, and the legatee accepted... Acceptance must be before revocation by the offeror; if he revokes all or part, it is invalid. And based on that is what is in al-Khaniyyah: If he said 'I sold you this for one thousand' then said to another 'I sold you half of it for five hundred', and the second was said [to accept], Abu Yusuf said: The acceptance of the second is valid, and the acceptance of the first is not valid after the seller's revocation of half. End quote. And if the acceptance came out... Then I checked another copy of al-Tatar Khaniyyah and found it as the author transmitted. His statement: (except) in his mention of Qadi Khan etc. He said in al-Nahr: This is an oversight, and apparently its source is the understanding that what is meant is the sale is valid, and it is not so, that he sells it by offer and acceptance. Then I saw the issue, and praise be to God, in Shuf'ah of al-Muhit: the acceptance of the will is valid, and the executor must act according to what I understood, where he said: He bequeathed that his house be sold to a man for one thousand dirhams, and the legatee accepted after his death, pre-emption becomes obligatory even if he did not take possession, because the will is conditional on consideration and it does not confer ownership except after taking possession. This is if the heir or executor offered the sale after his death and the legatee accepted. End quote. His statement: (And based on that is what is in al-Khaniyyah etc.) Possibly contradicting what is also in al-Khaniyyah in the chapter of invalid sale: A man sold a cloth at its marked price, then the seller sold it to another before clarifying the price, his sale to the second is valid; but if the seller informed the first of the price and he did not accept until the seller sold it to another, his sale to the second is not valid, because when the seller clarified the price, the sale became dependent on the first buyer's consent; unless the buyer consumed it after knowing the price, he owes the price; if he consumed it before knowing the price, he owes... Page 448: The book of sales. The sale as revocation of the offeror simultaneously, the revocation takes precedence as in al-Khaniyyah. And if offer and acceptance occur simultaneously, the sale is valid according to al-Tatar Khaniyyah. And it is not required that the acceptance include addressing after the offer is made with addressing; so if after he said 'I sold you', he said 'I bought' without saying 'from you', it is valid as in Fath al-Qadir. And if he said 'I sold it to you for one thousand' and he said 'I bought it for one thousand with a term of one year' or 'with a condition of option', it is not concluded unless he consents in the session; as in al-Mujtaba. And acceptance must be before a change in the sold item; and based on that is what is in al-Khaniyyah: If the hand of the slave-girl was cut after the offer and the seller took her diyah, or the slave-girl gave birth, or the grape juice fermented then turned to vinegar, the acceptance of the buyer is not valid. End quote. Likewise if the sold item was two slaves, one was killed by mistake and the seller took the diyah, acceptance is not valid; as in al-Zahiriyyah. And [acceptance] must be before the addressee rejects the offer; so if he said 'I sold you for one thousand' and he said 'I do not accept; rather I gave it for five hundred' then said 'I took it for one thousand', Abu Yusuf said: If he handed it over, then it is consent, otherwise not; as in al-Khaniyyah. And we have already stated in the explanation of conditions that acceptance must be in all that he offered with all that he offered; so acceptance of part or with part is not valid when the transaction is unitary, due to the necessity of dividing the transaction which requires a defect of partnership—not due to the custom of mixing good with bad to promote it as occurred in some books, for it does not include when the sold item is single and he accepts part, as in al-Ghayah. And it is necessary to know what requires its unity and division. The sum of what they mentioned is that if the offeror is single and the addressees are multiple, division by acceptance of one of them is not permissible, whether the offeror is seller or buyer; and conversely, acceptance of the share of one is not permissible; and if both are single, acceptance of part by the addressee is not valid; so division is absolutely not valid in the three situations: when the offeror is single or multiple, or the acceptor is single or multiple, due to the unity of the transaction in all. Likewise if the two contractors are single and the sold items are multiple, as when he offers two fungibles or a fungible and a non-fungible, division of them by acceptance of one is not valid unless the other consents after his acceptance of part, and the sold item is such that the price can be divided by apportionment—like a single slave or a measured or weighed item—then the acceptance becomes an offer and the consent an acceptance, and the first offer is void. If it is such that division is only by value, like two garments of value... end quote. So let it be considered. Then the answer appeared that this is after offer and acceptance by the buyer and before knowledge of the price, and our case is before acceptance. End quote. His statement: (And if offer and acceptance occur simultaneously, the sale is valid) attributed in al-Tatar Khaniyyah to al-Khulasah, who said: Thus my father used to say, but in al-Qahistani: And it should be that the waw in his words 'with offer and acceptance' is in the meaning of fa, for if they were simultaneous, it would not be concluded, as they said in salam. End quote. Its apparent meaning is that he analogized sale to salam, and al-Tajnis explicitly stated regarding our specific issue: A man said to another 'I sold you this slave for one thousand dirhams' and the other said 'I accept' and the seller said 'I revoke', and the two utterances came out simultaneously, the sale is not valid because what prevents the validity of acceptance accompanied it, which is the seller's revocation. End quote. His statement: (And the seller took her diyah) He said in al-Nahr: Apparently the restriction to taking the diyah is by agreement. End quote. I say: This is supported by what is in al-Tatar Khaniyyah from al-Zahiriyyah where it said: And whether he paid the diyah of the hand to the seller or not. His statement: (Rather I gave it for five hundred) with omission of the interrogative hamza and opening the ta of address.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a detailed commentary on the conditions and rulings of acceptance (qabul) in sale contracts. The author begins by discussing the validity of the word 'na'am' as acceptance. 'Na'am' after a question like 'Did you buy?' or 'Did you sell?' is considered a valid acceptance, but it is effective only if the price is paid (naqd) because payment confirms the seriousness of the transaction. The text then presents several scenarios from al-Khaniyyah illustrating how the last statement in a bargaining session determines the price. For example, if the buyer and seller express different prices and the buyer takes the item without further discussion, the contract is concluded at the price last stated by the party in whose possession the item was. If the item was in the buyer's hand during bargaining, the seller's last price applies; if in the seller's hand, the buyer's last offer applies. This shows the principle that in ambiguous situations, the final word is decisive. The commentary then moves to the essential condition that acceptance must occur in the same session (majlis) as the offer. If either party stands up, the offer is void according to the relied-upon view, though there is a minority view that as long as they remain in the place, the session continues. Speaking to another person about a need also invalidates the session. The offeror must be alive until acceptance; if he dies, the offer lapses except in a specific case mentioned by Qadi Khan regarding a bequest to sell. The text also discusses the requirement that the acceptance must cover the entire offer; partial acceptance is invalid if the transaction is unitary (safqah wahidah). This is because splitting the transaction would introduce a defect of partnership. The passage explains the three scenarios: single offeror with multiple addressees, multiple offerors with single addressee, and single offeror with single addressee—in all cases, acceptance of part is invalid. Exception: if the other party consents after a partial acceptance, and the sold item can be divided by apportionment (like a slave or measured goods), then the partial acceptance becomes a new offer and the consent an acceptance, voiding the original offer. The text also addresses simultaneous offer and acceptance: according to al-Tatar Khaniyyah, if both occur at the exact same time, the sale is valid, but al-Qahistani and others argue that 'simultaneous' should be understood as 'immediately consecutive' (with waw meaning fa) because true simultaneity would invalidate the contract, analogizing to salam. The final sections discuss change in the sold item before acceptance (like injury or transformation) and revocation by the offeror before acceptance, with Abu Yusuf's view on conditional language.

Key Terms
قبول (qabul): Acceptance of an offer in a sale contract; must be in the same session, cover the entire offer, and occur before any change in the sold item or revocation.
مجلس الإيجاب (majlis al-ijab): The session in which the offer is made; acceptance must take place in this same session for a valid contract.
صفقة واحدة (safqah wahidah): A unitary transaction where multiple items or rights are sold together as one bundle; partial acceptance is invalid because it divides the transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the buyer says 'I will not take it except for ten' and the seller says 'I will not sell except for fifteen', and then the buyer takes the item from the seller's hand and the seller does not stop him, what is the price?
A) Fifteen, because the seller's last statement controls.
B) Ten, because the buyer's last offer controls when the seller passively hands over.
C) The price is undetermined and the sale is invalid.
D) Ten unless the seller explicitly agrees to fifteen.

Key Takeaway
Acceptance in a sale must be in the same session, cover all that was offered, and occur before revocation or any change in the sold item; otherwise the sale is void.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
7 min
Conditions for Valid Acceptance (Qabul) in Sale
States conditions for qabul: must be before change in mabi', before rejection, and must accept entire offer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three main conditions for a valid acceptance in a Hanafi sale contract and apply them to scenarios involving changes to the subject matter, rejection, and partial acceptance.

Core Idea
Acceptance must match the entire offer, precede any change in the goods, and come before the offeror's rejection.

This lesson examines the Hanafi conditions that validate an acceptance (qabul) in a sale contract. While the offer sets the terms, the acceptance must meet specific requirements to form a binding agreement. The text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq outlines these conditions with illustrative examples from the classical sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its conditions
Acceptance (qabul) is a rukn of the sale. The text lists conditions for its validity: (1) no need for direct address, (2) before change in mabi', (3) before rejection, (4) must cover entire offer.
2
Examine the 'no direct address' and conditional acceptance rule
Saying 'I bought' suffices. But adding a condition like 'until a year' makes it incomplete until the offeror agrees in the session.
This shows acceptance must be unconditional to be valid.
3
Examine the 'before change in mabi' condition
Examples: if the slave-girl's hand is cut, she gives birth, juice ferments, or one slave is killed, acceptance after such change is invalid.
The subject matter must remain as offered.
4
Examine the 'before rejection' condition and Abu Yusuf's view
If the offeror rejects, later acceptance is invalid. Abu Yusuf holds that payment of price indicates consent.
The relied-upon position is the stricter one.
5
Understand the unity of transaction rule
Acceptance of part of a single transaction is invalid unless the other party agrees after the acceptance, and the item is divisible by parts (e.g., a single slave, measured goods).
Key concept: safqah (transaction) unity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يشترط أن يشتمل القبول على الخطاب بعدما صدر الإيجاب بالخطاب فلو قال بعد قوله بعتك اشتريت ولم يقل منك صح كما في فتح القدير. ولو قال بعتكه بألف فقال اشتريته بألف إلى سنة أو بشرط الخيار لم يتم إلا إذا رضي في المجلس؛ كذا في المجتبى. ولا بد من كون القبول قبل تغير المبيع وعليه تفرع ما في الخانية : لو قطعت يد الجارية بعد الإيجاب وأخذ البائع أرشها أو ولدت الجارية أو تخمر العصير ثم صار خلاً لم يصح قبول المشتري .اهـ. وكذا لو كان المبيع عبدين فقتل أحدهما خطأ وأخذ البائع الأرش لم يجز القبول؛ كذا في الظهيرية ولا بد أن يكون قبل رد المخاطب الإيجاب، فلو قال بعتك بألف فقال لا أقبل بل أعطيته بخمسمائة ثم قال أخذته بألف قال أبو يوسف : إن دفعه إليه فهو رضا وإلا فلا كذا في الخانية. وقدمنا في بيان الشرائط أنه لا بد أن يكون القبول في جميع ما أوجب بجميع ما أوجبه فلم يصح القبول في البعض أو بالبعض حيث كانت الصفقة متحدة للزوم تفريق الصفقة المقتضي لعيب الشركة لا من جهة جريان العادة بضم الجيد إلى الرديء ليروج كما وقع في بعض الكتب فإنه لا يشمل ما إذا كان المبيع واحداً فقبل في بعض البعض كما في الغاية ولا بد من معرفة يوجب اتحادها وتفريقها. وحاصل ما ذكروه أن الموجب إذا اتحد وتعدد المخاطب لم يجز التفريق بقبول أحدهما، بائعاً كان الموجب أو مشترياً، وعلى عكسه لم يجز القبول في حصة أحدهما، وإن اتحدا لم يصح قبول المخاطب في البعض فلم يصح تفريقها مطلقاً في الأحوال الثلاثة أعني ما إذا اتحد الموجب أو تعدد أو اتحد القابل أو تعدد لاتحاد الصفقة في الكل، وكذا إذا اتحد العاقدان وتعدد المبيع كأن يوجب في مثليين أو قيمي ومثلي لم يجز تفريقها بالقبول في أحدهما إلا أن يرضى الآخر بذلك بعد قبوله في البعض، ويكون المبيع مما ينقسم الثمن عليه بالإجزاء كعبد واحد أو مكيل أو موزون فيكون القبول إيجاباً والرضا قبولاً وبطل الإيجاب الأول، فإن كان مما لا ينقسم إلا بالقيمة كثوبين وعبدين لا يجوز.
And it is not required that the acceptance includes the address after the offer has been made with address, so if after his saying 'I sold to you' he says 'I bought' and did not say 'from you', it is valid, as in Fath al-Qadir. And if he said 'I sold it to you for a thousand' and he said 'I bought it for a thousand until a year' or 'with a condition of option', it is not completed unless he agrees in the session; as in al-Mujtaba. And it is necessary that the acceptance be before a change in the sold item, and on that branches what is in al-Khaniyya: if after the offer the hand of the slave-girl is cut and the seller takes her compensation, or the slave-girl gives birth, or the juice ferments and then becomes vinegar, the acceptance of the buyer is not valid. And similarly if the sold item were two slaves and one is killed by mistake and the seller takes the compensation, acceptance is not valid; as in al-Zuhayriyya. And it must be before the addressee rejects the offer, so if he said 'I sold to you for a thousand' and he said 'I do not accept, rather I give it for five hundred' then said 'I take it for a thousand', Abu Yusuf said: if he paid it, it is consent, otherwise not; as in al-Khaniyya. And we have presented in the exposition of conditions that it is necessary that the acceptance be for all that he offered with all that he offered, so acceptance of part or with part is not valid when the transaction is single, due to the necessity of splitting the transaction which necessitates a defect of partnership, not from the angle of the custom of joining good to bad to promote sales as occurred in some books, for it does not include the case where the sold item is one and he accepts part of some, as in al-Ghaya. And it is necessary to know what determines its unity and its splitting. The summary of what they mentioned is that when the offeror is single and the addressees are multiple, splitting by the acceptance of one of them is not permissible, whether the offeror is a seller or buyer; and on the contrary, acceptance for the share of one of them is not permissible; and if both are single, the acceptance of the addressee for part is not valid. So its splitting is not valid absolutely in the three cases: i.e., whether the offeror is single or multiple, or the acceptor is single or multiple, due to the unity of the transaction in all. And similarly if the two contractors are single and the sold items are multiple, as if he offers two fungibles or a fungible and a qimi, splitting by acceptance in one of them is not permissible unless the other agrees to that after his acceptance of part, and the sold item is such that the price can be divided on it by parts, like a single slave or a measure or a weight; then the acceptance becomes an offer and the consent becomes an acceptance, and the first offer becomes void. As for what cannot be divided except by value, like two garments and two slaves, it is not permissible.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the conditions for the validity of acceptance (qabul) in a sale contract. The author first states that the acceptance does not need to include a direct address to the offeror; saying 'I bought' suffices. Then he states that acceptance must occur before any change in the sold item, such as the animal giving birth or the slave girl's hand being severed and compensation taken. It also must occur before the offeror rejects the offer. Finally, it must be in response to the entire offer; acceptance of part of a single transaction is invalid. The reason given is that splitting a single transaction causes a defect of partnership (عيب الشركة). The author then details the application to cases of single or multiple parties.

Key Terms
قَبُول (qabul): Acceptance in a contract; the second statement that completes the contract.
صَفْقَة (safqah): A transaction; the entire deal including all items and price.
مُوجِب (mujib): The person who makes the offer (ijab) in a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is acceptance of part of a single transaction valid?
A) When the other party agrees to the split after the original acceptance.
B) Never, it is always invalid.
C) Only if the sold item is a fungible (mithli).
D) Only if the price is specified for each part.

Key Takeaway
Acceptance must be unconditional, timely (before change or rejection), and cover the entire offer; any deviation requires the offeror's explicit re-consent.

Effect of Specifying Prices on Unity of Transaction
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of price specification on transaction unity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether specifying prices creates separate transactions and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Specifying separate prices may indicate separate transactions, but Abu Hanifa requires repeating the sale phrase; the Sahibayn suffice with price specification.

When a seller offers multiple items in one statement, does specifying a separate price for each create multiple contracts or a single one? This question arises frequently in sales of bundles or multiple goods. The Hanafi school has an internal difference: Imam Abu Hanifa insists on repeating the sale phrase for each item, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, hold that price specification alone suffices. This lesson unpacks that dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between repeating the sale phrase (takrar lafz al-bay') and merely specifying prices without repetition. With repetition, there is consensus that multiple transactions are formed. Without repetition, the dispute arises.
This scenario is the core of the disagreement.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that without repeating the phrase, the transaction is singular. His reasoning is based on istihsan (juristic preference) – custom and practice indicate that repetition is needed to separate deals.
Istihsan departs from strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of custom.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that specifying prices shows the seller's intention to sell each item separately, so multiple transactions are formed even without repetition. This is qiyas (analogy) based on the meaning of the offer.
Qiyas here uses the intention inferred from price differentiation.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Later authorities, including Fath al-Qadir, prefer the Sahibayn's view. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that price specification alone creates multiple contracts.
The tarjih (preference) is based on the apparent benefit of price specification.
5
Note the restriction on divisible goods
The passage adds an important limitation: price specification only creates separate contracts if the items are divided by value. If they are divisible by quantity (like identical measures), specification does not create multiple contracts.
This restriction is from Sharh al-Majma' and is accepted as sound (taqyid hasan).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو بين ثمن كل واحد فلا يخلو إما أن يكون بلا تكرار لفظ البيع أو بتكراره، ففيما إذا كرره فالاتفاق على أنه صفقتان، فإذا قبل في أحدهما يصح مثل أن يقول بعتك هذين العبدين بعتك هذا بألف وهذا بألفين وفيما إذا لم يكرره وفصل الثمن فظاهر الهداية التعدد وبه قال بعضهم ومنعه الآخرون وحملوا كلامه على ما إذا كرر لفظ البيع. وقيل : إن اشتراط تكرار لفظ البيع للتعدد استحسان وهو قول الإمام، وعدمه قياس، وهو قولهما. ورجح في فتح القدير قولهما بقوله والوجه الاكتفاء بمجرد تفريق الثمن لأن الظاهر أن فائدته ليس إلا قصده بأن يبيع منه أيهما شاء وإلا فلو كان غرضه أن لا يبيعهما منه إلا جملة لم تكن فائدة لتعيين ثمن كل واحد منهما .اهـ. واعلم أن تفصيل الثمن إنما يجعلهما عقدين على القول به إذا كان الثمن منقسماً عليهما باعتبار القيمة أما إذا كان منقسماً عليهما باعتبار الأجزاء كالقفيزين من جنس واحد فإن التفصيل لا يجعله في حكم عقدين للانقسام من غير تفصيل فلم يعتبر التفصيل كما في شرح المجمع للمصنف وهو تقييد حسن.
If he specifies the price of each one, then it is either without repetition of the sale phrase or with its repetition. In the case where he repeats it, there is agreement that they are two transactions; if he accepts one of them, it is valid, like if he says: 'I sold you these two slaves, I sold you this one for a thousand and this one for two thousand.' In the case where he does not repeat it and specifies the price, then the apparent meaning of al-Hidayah is multiplicity, and some said that, and others prevented it and interpreted his words as applying to when he repeats the sale phrase. And it is said that requiring repetition of the sale phrase for multiplicity is istihsan, and that is the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa; and not requiring it is qiyas, and that is the saying of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And in Fath al-Qadir, their saying is preferred with his words: 'The correct view is to suffice with mere differentiation of the price, because the apparent benefit is nothing but his intention to sell whichever he wishes from them; otherwise, if his purpose was not to sell them both to him except as a lot, there would be no benefit in specifying the price of each one.' Know that specification of the price makes them two contracts according to that view only if the price is divided between them by way of value. As for if it is divided between them by way of parts, like two qafizes of the same kind, then specification does not make them in the ruling of two contracts, because they are divisible without specification, so specification is not considered, as in Sharh al-Majma' by the author, and that is a good restriction.

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the effect of specifying separate prices for multiple items in a single offer on whether they become separate transactions. The author presents the intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa (istihsan) holds that repetition of the sale phrase (like saying 'I sold you this for X, I sold you that for Y') is necessary for multiple transactions; without repetition, it remains one transaction. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (qiyas) hold that merely specifying the prices suffices to create multiple transactions, as this indicates the seller's intention to sell each item separately. The commentator notes that the author of Fath al-Qadir prefers the view of the Sahibayn. An important restriction is added: specification of prices only creates separate contracts if the items are divided by value, not if they are divisible by mere quantity (like two identical measures).

Key Terms
تَكْرَار لَفْظ البَيْع (takrar lafz al-bay'): Repeating the phrase 'I sold you' for each item separately.
تَفْصِيل الثَّمَن (tafsil al-thaman): Specifying the price for each item individually.
اِسْتِحْسَان (istihsan): Juristic preference departing from qiyas due to custom or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the preferred view (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, what suffices to create multiple transactions from a single offer?

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that specifying separate prices for multiple items creates separate contracts, even without repeating the sale phrase, as preferred by the Sahibayn and later authorities.

Non-Splitting Rule in Possession, Lease, and Partition
Extends non-splitting rule to possession, lease, partition, and lists exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule of non-splitting in possession, ijara, and qisma, and identify the exceptions where splitting is permissible.

Core Idea
Splitting a single transaction is invalid in sale, possession, lease, and partition, but valid in marriage and blood settlement.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq extends the principle that a single transaction cannot be split into parts. The rule applies not only to the contract itself but also to the act of taking possession, and to lease and partition contracts. However, certain contracts like marriage and khul' are exceptions where partial acceptance is valid. Understanding these boundaries is crucial for correctly executing transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base rule
Recognise that a single transaction (safqa) cannot be split; it must be accepted or rejected as a whole. This rule is established for sale.
Safqa refers to a single contractual exchange.
2
Apply the rule to possession (qabd)
When the transaction is single, the buyer cannot take partial possession even after paying part of the price. Possession must be complete.
Multiple scenarios are given: partial payment, set-off, presence of multiple buyers.
3
Extend to ijara and qisma
Lease and partition are treated like sale: splitting the transaction is invalid. For example, leasing for two months and accepting only one month is invalid.
Qisma (partition) is a contract of exchange.
4
Recognise exceptions
Marriage (nikah), khul', settlement for blood, and emancipation for payment allow partial acceptance. The reasoning is that these contracts are not purely commutative.
Combining marriage with sale: accepting marriage is valid, but accepting sale is not.
5
Note the reversal for multiple transactions
When the transactions are multiple (e.g., two separate sales), splitting is permissible. The rulings reverse accordingly.
The text cites al-Tatarakhaniyya for these details.

Source Text

وإذا كانت الصفقة متحدة لم يجز التفريق في القبض أيضاً، فلو تعدد المبيع ونقد بعض الثمن لم يجز أن يقبض بعض المبيع، فإن تعددت الصفقة جاز وحكم الإبراء عن البعض كالاستيفاء، وكذا إذا أجل ثمن بعض المبيع دون البعض لم يكن له أن يقبض شيئاً من المبيع حتى ينقد الحال، وكذا لو كان للمشتري على البائع دين أقل من الثمن فالتقيا قصاصاً بقدره لم يكن له أن يقبض شيئاً من المبيع حتى يأخذ الباقي كما في التتارخانية ويتفرع أيضاً ما لو حضر أحد المشتريين وغاب الآخر فنقد الحاضر حصته لم يكن له قبض شيء من المبيع حتى ينقد الغائب أو هو الجميع وقام الشريك مقام الغائب في حبس حصة الغائب حتى يدفع له ما عليه، فإن هلك المبيع قبل طلب الغائب هلك أمانة، فإذا حضر الغائب رجع عليه، وإن هلك بعد طلبه وحبسه للاستيفاء هلك أمانة بثمنه فلا رجوع على الغائب. ولو أبرأ البائع أحدهما عن حصته من الثمن أو أخره لم يكن له أن يقبض حصته من المبيع حتى ينقد الآخر، وأما إذا تعددت في هذه المسائل انعكست الأحكام؛ كذا في التتارخانية . ثم اعلم أن الإجارة والقسمة كالبيع لا يجوز فيهما تفريق الصفقة حتى لو أجر عبده شهرين بكذا فقبل في أحدهما لم يجز، وكذا لو قال قاسمتك هذا الرقيق الأربعة على أن هذين لي وهذين لك فقال الآخر سلمت لك هذا ولا أسلم لك هذا الآخر لم يجز، ويجوز هذا في النكاح والخلع والصلح عن دم والعتق على مال ولو جمع بين النكاح والبيع فقبل أحدهما، إن قبل النكاح جاز، وإن قبل البيع لم يجز. ولو جمع عتقاً وطلاقاً أو عتقاً ونكاحاً أو طلاقاً ونكاحاً جاز قبول أحدهما، ولو جمع مكاتبة وعتقاً وبين حصة المكاتبة جاز أيهما قبل وإن لم يبين لم يجز قبول الكتابة. ولو كان لرجل على رجل دم عمد بأن قتل أخويه فقال لمن عليه صالحتك منهما على عشرة آلاف فقال رضيت عن دم فلان بخمسة آلاف صح. وله أن يقتل الآخر.
And when the transaction is single, splitting is not permissible in possession either. So if the sold items are multiple and he pays part of the price, he may not take possession of part of the sold items. If the transactions are multiple, it is permissible. And the ruling of release (ibra') from part is like receiving. Similarly, if he defers the price of some of the sold items without others, he may not take possession of anything from the sold items until he pays the cash. Similarly, if the buyer has a debt on the seller less than the price, and they meet each other by way of set-off to that extent, he may not take possession of anything from the sold items until he takes the remainder, as in al-Tatarakhaniyya. And also derived from this: if one of two buyers is present and the other is absent, and the present one pays his share, he may not take possession of anything from the sold items until the absent one pays, or he pays all, and the partner takes the place of the absent one in detaining the share of the absent one until he pays what is due. If the sold item is destroyed before the request of the absent one, it is destroyed as a trust; when the absent one arrives, he has recourse against him. If it is destroyed after his request and his detention for collection, it is destroyed as a trust for its price, so there is no recourse against the absent one. And if the seller releases one of them from his share of the price or defers it, he may not take possession of his share of the sold items until the other pays. As for when the transactions are multiple, the rulings are reversed; as in al-Tatarakhaniyya. Then know that lease (ijara) and partition (qisma) are like sale: splitting the transaction is not permissible in them. So if he leased his slave for two months for a certain amount and the other accepts one month, it is not valid. Similarly, if he said: 'I partition these four slaves with you on the basis that these two are for me and these two for you' and the other says: 'I agree to this one for you but I do not agree to this other one', it is not valid. But this is permissible in marriage (nikah), khul', settlement for blood, and emancipation for payment. And if he combines marriage and sale and accepts one of them: if he accepts marriage, it is valid; if he accepts sale, it is not. And if he combines emancipation and divorce, or emancipation and marriage, or divorce and marriage, accepting one of them is valid. And if he combines kitabah and emancipation and specifies the share of kitabah, whichever he accepts is valid; if he does not specify, accepting the kitabah is not valid. And if a man has a claim of intentional killing on another man, for example he killed his two brothers, and he says to the one liable: 'I settle with you for both for ten thousand' and he says: 'I am satisfied for the blood of so-and-so for five thousand', it is valid. And he may kill the other.

Commentary
This passage extends the principle of non-splitting of a single transaction to the act of possession (qabd) and to other contracts. When the transaction is single, the buyer cannot take partial possession even if he pays part of the price. The author gives detailed scenarios involving multiple buyers, set-off, and payment of part. The rule is reversed when the transactions are multiple. Then the author states that the same prohibition applies to lease (ijara) and partition (qisma). However, exceptions are made for marriage (nikah), khul', settlement for blood money, and emancipation for payment (kitabah and 'itq bi mal), where partial acceptance is valid. Examples are given: combining marriage and sale—accepting marriage is valid but accepting sale is not; combining emancipation and divorce—both are valid separately; settlement for intentional killing—partial settlement is valid and the remaining blood remains actionable.

Key Terms
قَبْض (qabd): Possession or taking delivery of the sold item.
إِجَارَة (ijara): Lease or hire contract.
قِسْمَة (qisma): Partition of jointly owned property.
خُلْع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife with compensation to the husband.
صُلْح عَنْ دَم (sulh 'an dam): Settlement for blood money in cases of homicide.
عِتْق عَلَى مَال ('itq bi mal): Emancipation of a slave in exchange for payment.
صَفْقَة (safqa): A transaction or contractual exchange. Often used to denote a single bargain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Lease (ijara)
C) Marriage (nikah)

Key Takeaway
The rule that a single transaction cannot be split applies to sale, possession, lease, and partition, but not to marriage, khul', blood settlement, or emancipation for payment.

Exception to Binding Sale After an Invalid Contract
Explains exception when offer/acceptance occur after an abandoned invalid contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exception to the binding nature of a sale after a fasid contract and apply it to distinguish between a fasid sale that has been abandoned and one that has not.

Core Idea
A new sale after an abandoned fasid contract is valid; otherwise it is invalid (batil).

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a critical exception to the general rule that a sale becomes binding upon offer and acceptance. The exception arises when a prior invalid (fasid) contract exists and has not been abandoned by the parties. The author then illustrates the rule with two cases from al-Khaniyyah, showing how the status of the prior contract determines the validity of the subsequent transaction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule and the Exception
The general rule is that a sale becomes binding (lazim) upon offer and acceptance. The exception: if offer and acceptance occur after a fasid contract that the parties did not abandon, the new sale is not binding—in fact, it is invalid (batil).
The key phrase is 'لم يتركاه' (they did not abandon it).
2
Study the First Case from al-Khaniyyah
A person buys a garment in a fasid sale. The next day, he says 'You sold me this garment for 1000' and the seller agrees, and he says 'I have taken it.' The second transaction is invalid because it is built upon the prior fasid sale that was not abandoned. If the parties had abandoned the first fasid sale, the new transaction would be valid.
Note the condition: 'إذا لم يتركاه' (if they did not abandon it).
3
Analyze the Second Case: Conditional Sale
A seller says: 'If you bring the price today, the slave is yours; if not, no sale.' The buyer accepts but does not pay. The next day, the buyer says 'You sold me this slave for 1000' and the seller agrees. This second transaction is a valid new purchase because the first conditional sale was annulled (muntadis) by the failure of the condition. It differs from a fasid contract that remains in effect.
The dissolution is automatic due to the condition; no need for explicit abandonment.
4
Understand the Distinction: Fasid vs. Annulled
A fasid sale continues to exist until abandoned; it taints a subsequent contract. An annulled sale (due to a dissolving condition) leaves no legal trace, so a new transaction is independent.
The author notes that even with khiyar al-naqd (option of payment), the sale becomes fasid but does not automatically dissolve.
5
Apply the Ruling to New Scenarios
Given a scenario, first identify if there was a prior fasid contract. If yes, check whether it was abandoned. If abandoned, the new sale is valid; otherwise, it is invalid.
Remember: 'إذا حصلا بعد عقد فاسد لم يتركاه' (if they occur after a fasid contract that they did not abandon).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستثنى من قوله يلزم بإيجاب وقبول ما إذا حصلا بعد عقد فاسد لم يتركاه فإن البيع ليس بلازم، ويتفرع عليه ما في الخانية : لو اشترى ثوباً شراء فاسداً ثم لقيه غداً فقال قد بعتني ثوبك هذا بألف فقال بلى فقال قد أخذته فهو باطل . وهذا على ما كان قبله من البيع الفاسد، فإن كانا تتاركا البيع الفاسد فهو جائز اليوم ولو باع عبداً من رجل بألف درهم وقال إن جئتني اليوم بالثمن فهو لك وإن لم تجئني اليوم بالثمن فلا بيع بيني وبينك فقبل المشتري ولم يأته بالثمن فلقيه غداً فقال المشتري قد بعتني عبدك هذا بألف فقال فقال قد أخذته فهو شراء الساعة لأن ذلك الشراء قد انتقض ولم يشبه هذا البيع الفاسد .اهـ. مع أن البيع يفسد إذا كان فيه خيار نقد ولم ينقد حتى مضى الوقت حتى قالوا بفساده وعدم انفساخه حتى لو كان عبداً في يد المشتري وأعتقه صح فينبغي أن لا فرق لأن الفرع الثاني من أفراد البيع الفاسد، وقدمنا أن البائع إذا قبل بأقل مما أوجبه المشتري صح وكان خطأ وأن المشتري إذا قبل بأزيد وكان زيادة إن قبلها في المجلس لزمت
And there is an exception from his saying 'it is binding by offer and acceptance' when they occur after an invalid contract that they did not abandon: then the sale is not binding. Branched from it is what is in al-Khaniyyah: If someone bought a garment in an invalid purchase, then met him the next day and said, 'You sold me this garment for a thousand,' and he said, 'Yes,' and he said, 'I have taken it,' then it is invalid. And this depends on what was before of the invalid sale. If they abandoned the invalid sale, then it is valid today. And if he sold a slave to a man for a thousand dirhams and said, 'If you bring me the price today, it is yours; if you do not bring me the price today, then no sale between me and you,' and the buyer accepted but did not bring the price, then met him the next day and the buyer said, 'You sold me this slave of yours for a thousand,' and he said, 'I have taken it,' then it is a purchase of the hour because that purchase was annulled and it did not resemble this invalid sale. End. Although the sale is invalid if there is an option of payment and he did not pay until the time passed, so they said it is invalid and does not dissolve, so much so that if the slave was in the buyer's hand and he emancipated him, it is valid, so there should be no difference because the second branch is an instance of invalid sale. And we previously stated that if the seller accepts less than what the buyer offered, it is valid and was a mistake, and if the buyer accepts more and it is an increase, if he accepts it in the session it is binding.
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with detailed case analysis. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains an exception to the general principle that a sale is binding upon offer and acceptance. The exception occurs when the offer and acceptance happen after a fasid (invalid) contract that the parties have not abandoned. In that case, the new sale is not binding because it is built upon the invalid contract. He then branches two cases from al-Khaniyyah. First: if someone buys a garment in a fasid sale, then the next day says 'you sold me this garment for 1000' and the seller agrees and the buyer says 'I have taken it', the second transaction is invalid because it is based on the prior fasid sale. However, if the parties had abandoned the first fasid sale, then the new transaction is valid (ja'iz). Second: a conditional sale where the seller says 'if you bring the price today, the slave is yours; otherwise no sale'. The buyer accepts but does not pay. The next day the buyer says 'you sold me this slave for 1000' and the seller agrees and the buyer says 'I have taken it'. In this case, the second is a new valid purchase because the first conditional sale was annulled (intaqada) when the condition failed—it is not like a fasid sale. The author then notes a nuance: normally a sale with a deferred payment option (khiyar al-naqd) is fasid and does not dissolve automatically when the time expires; it remains fasid. So the emancipated slave example would be valid even though the sale is fasid. Therefore, the second branch (conditional sale) should also be fasid? But the author explains the difference: in the conditional case, the condition "if you do not bring the price, no sale" makes the sale void (muntadis) rather than merely fasid, so it is different. The text then reiterates a prior ruling about accepting less or more than the offer.

Key Terms
عقد فاسد (aql fāsid): A contract that is legally defective in its conditions or pillars, but not entirely void (batil); here it refers to a sale that lacks some requirement (e.g., delayed payment without specifying time).
خيار نقد (khiyār naqd): Option of paying the price within a specified time; if payment is not made, the sale may become fasid.
إيجاب وقبول (ījāb wa qabūl): Offer and acceptance; the essential components (rukns) of a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case from al-Khaniyyah, if a person buys a garment in a fasid sale, then the next day says 'You sold me this garment for 1000' and the seller agrees and the buyer says 'I have taken it', why is this second transaction invalid?
A) Because the offer and acceptance were not in the same session.
B) Because it is built upon the prior fasid sale that was not abandoned.
C) Because the seller did not accept the offer in the proper form.
D) Because the price was not specified clearly.

Key Takeaway
A new offer and acceptance after a fasid contract is only valid if the parties have abandoned the fasid contract; otherwise, it is invalid (batil).

Offer and Acceptance via Writing and Messenger
Ruling with proof on offer through writing and messenger

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for concluding a contract through written offer or messenger, identify which contracts require acceptance in the same council for both halves, and apply the rulings on withdrawal before delivery.

Core Idea
A written offer is like speech; the contract is concluded when acceptance occurs in the council of receipt, except when the half depends on later acceptance.

The Hanafi school equates written and messenger-based offers to spoken offers, but the council of acceptance is the moment the writing is received or the messenger delivers the message. This lesson unpacks the implications: which contracts require the accepting party to respond in that same council, and which contracts leave one half pending until later acceptance. We also examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on marriage and the rules for withdrawing an offer before delivery.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the equivalence of writing and messenger to speech
The passage begins by stating that writing and sending a messenger are like direct speech. Understand that the legal effect is the same: the offer is considered communicated when the writing reaches the addressee or the messenger delivers the message.
The council of receipt (majlis al-bulugh) is the analogue of the council of a verbal offer.
2
Identify the contracts and their categories
List the contracts mentioned: sale (bay'), hire (ijarah), gift (hibah), kitaba (contract of manumission), khul', manumission for payment (itaq 'ala mal), and marriage (nikah). Classify them based on whether the half (shatr) depends on acceptance after the council.
Sale, hire, gift, kitaba, and marriage (according to the two) do not have a dependent half. Khul' and manumission for payment do have a dependent half (by consensus).
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on marriage
Note the difference between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two) and Abu Yusuf. The two hold that marriage does not require acceptance in the same council; Abu Yusuf holds that it does. This affects the validity of a marriage proposal by writing when acceptance occurs later.
The passage sides with the two, indicating the relied-upon view.
4
Apply the ruling on withdrawal and conditioning
For contracts where the half does not depend, the offering party may withdraw before acceptance and cannot attach conditions. For contracts where it does depend (like khul'), withdrawal is invalid and conditioning is valid because it is treated like an oath from one side.
This distinction stems from the nature of the contract: commutative vs. semi-oath.
5
Differentiate between withdrawal from the message and dismissal of the messenger
The passage from Fath al-Qadir allows the writer/messenger to withdraw before delivery, even without the other party's knowledge. However, according to al-Bazzaziyyah, formally dismissing the messenger requires his knowledge. Understand the practical difference.
Withdrawal revokes the offer; dismissal ends the messenger's agency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشمل كلامه الإيجاب والقبول بالكتابة والرسالة . قال في الهداية والكتاب كالخطاب وكذا الإرسال حتى اعتبر مجلس بلوغ الكتاب وأداء الرسالة. وصورة الكتاب أن يكتب : أما بعد فقد بعت عبدي فلاناً منك بكذا فلما بلغه الكتاب قال في مجلسه ذلك اشتريت تم البيع بينهما وصورة الإرسال أن يرسل رسولاً فيقول البائع بعت هذا فلان الغائب بألف . فاذهب يا فلان فقل له، فذهب الرسول فأخبره بما قال فقبل المشتري في مجلسه ذلك. وفي النهاية وكذا هذا الجواب في الإجارة والهبة والكتابة. فأما في الخلع والعتق على مال فإنه يتوقف شطر العقد من الزوج والمولى على قبول الآخر وراء المجلس بالإجماع بخلاف البيع والشراء فإنه لا يتوقف، فإن من قال عبدي هذا فلان الغائب بكذا وبلغه الخبر فقبل لا يصح لأن شطر العقد لا يتوقف فيه من [؟] صح [؟] بالإجماع، فأما في النكاح فلا يتوقف الشطر عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف. ثم في كل موضع لا يتوقف شطر العقد فإنه يجوز من العاقد الرجوع عنه ولا يجوز تعليقه بالشروط لأنه عقد معاوضة، وفي كل موضع يتوقف كالخلع لا يصح الرجوع ويصح التعليق بالشرط لكونه يميناً من جانب الزوج والمولى معاوضة من جانب الزوجة والعبد اهـ. وفي فتح القدير: ويصح الرجوع من المكاتب والمرسل قبل الوصول، سواء علم الآخر أو لم يعلم. وفي غاية البيان معزياً إلى مبسوط شيخ الإسلام الخطاب والكتاب سواء إلا في فصل واحد وهو قوله : (مع أن البيع يفسد الخ) أي بناء على ما صححه في الخانية أيضاً من أنه لو لم ينقد في المدة يفسد ولا ينفسخ كما سيذكره المؤلف في باب خيار الشرط، وحينئذ فلا منافاة بين الفرعين لأن الفرع الثاني مبني على مقابل الصحيح من أنه ينفسخ ولا يفسد ولهذا قال: لأن ذلك الشراء قد انتقض الخ. تأمل قوله : (لأن الغائب إنما صار مخاطباً لها بالكتاب الذي في غاية البيان خاطباً من الخطبة وتمام العبارة بعد قوله وهو باقٍ في المجلس الثاني فصار بقاء الكتاب في مجلسه وقد سمع الشهود ما في الكتاب في المجلس الثاني بمنزلة ما لو تكرر الخطاب من الحاضر في مجلس آخر، فأما [؟] [؟] . وفي النهاية معزياً إلى شرح الطحاوي: يصح الرجوع عن الرسالة علم الرسول أو لم يعلم اهـ. وفي وكالة البزازية والخلاصة : لا يصح عزل الرسول بدون علمه اهـ. فعلى هذا يفرق بين الرجوع والعزل
And his speech included the offer and acceptance by writing and sending a messenger. He said in al-Hidayah: Writing is like speech, and likewise sending a messenger, to the extent that the council of the arrival of the writing and the performance of the message are considered. The form of writing: that he writes: 'To proceed: I have sold my slave so-and-so to you for such amount.' When the writing reaches him, he says in that council 'I bought', the sale is concluded between them. The form of sending a messenger: that he sends a messenger and the seller says 'I have sold this absent person so-and-so for a thousand. Go, so-and-so, and tell him.' So the messenger goes and informs him of what he said, and the buyer accepts in that council. And in al-Nihayah: likewise this answer applies to hire, gift, and kitaba. As for khul' and manumission for payment, then half of the contract from the husband and master depends on the acceptance of the other outside the council by consensus, unlike sale and purchase, for which it does not depend. For if someone says 'my slave this absent person for such amount' and the news reaches him and he accepts, it is not valid because half of the contract does not depend on it... by consensus. As for marriage, the half does not depend according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf. Then, in every place where the half does not depend, the contracting party may withdraw from it and it is not permissible to condition it, because it is a commutative contract. And in every place where it depends, like khul', withdrawal is not valid and conditioning is valid because it is an oath on the husband's and master's side and a commutative contract from the wife's and slave's side. End. And in Fath al-Qadir: It is permissible for the writer and the sender to withdraw before arrival, whether the other knows or does not know. And in Ghaayat al-Bayan, attributed to the Mabsoot of Shaykh al-Islam: The writing and the book are the same except in one chapter, which is his statement: 'although the sale is invalid...' meaning based on what was corrected in al-Khaniyyah also, that if he did not pay within the time, it becomes invalid and does not dissolve, as the author will mention in the chapter on khiyar al-shart. Then there is no inconsistency between the two branches because the second branch is built on the opposite of the correct view, that it dissolves and does not become invalid, and therefore he said: 'that purchase had been annulled...' Contemplate his statement: 'Because the absent person has become addressed to her by the writing...' in Ghaayat al-Bayan... And in al-Nihayah, attributed to Sharh al-Tahawi: It is permissible to withdraw from the message whether the messenger knew or did not know. End. And in the Wakalah of al-Bazzaziyyah and al-Khulasa: It is not valid to dismiss the messenger without his knowledge. End. Therefore, one distinguishes between withdrawal and dismissal.
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage expands on the ruling that offer and acceptance can be made via writing or a messenger. The principle from al-Hidayah is that writing and speech are equivalent; the council (majlis) of receiving the writing or the messenger's message is the effective council. Two forms are illustrated: (1) Writing: the seller writes an offer; when the buyer receives the writing and accepts in that council, the sale is concluded. (2) Messenger: the seller tells a messenger to convey the offer to an absent buyer; when the messenger delivers it and the buyer accepts in that council, the sale is concluded. The same applies to hire (ijarah), gift (hibah), and kitabah (contract of manumission). However, for khul' and itaq 'ala mal (manumission for payment), one side (the husband/mawla) depends on the other's acceptance after the council, by consensus; for marriage, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it does not depend (contrary to Abu Yusuf). Then there is an important distinction: in contracts where one side does not depend (like sale), the party can withdraw before acceptance and cannot condition it; in contracts where it depends (like khul'), withdrawal is invalid and conditioning is valid because it is like an oath from one side and a commutative contract from the other. The passage also discusses withdrawal from the writing/messenger before delivery: according to Fath al-Qadir, it is valid whether the other knows or not; but according to al-Bazzaziyyah, dismissing the messenger without his knowledge is invalid. Thus a distinction is drawn between simply withdrawing the message (valid) and formally dismissing the messenger (requires knowledge).

Key Terms
شطر العقد (shaṭr al-ʿaqd): Half of the contract; meaning the part of the contract that emanates from one party (e.g., the offer or acceptance).
مجلس بلوغ الكتاب (majlis bulūgh al-kitāb): The council or session in which the written offer is received by the addressee; acceptance must occur in this council for the contract to be concluded.
رجوع (rujūʿ): Withdrawal; the act of revoking an offer before it is accepted.
عزل (ʿazl): Dismissal; removing the messenger from his agency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, in which contract does half of the contract depend on the other party's acceptance outside the council by consensus?
A) Sale (bay')
B) Marriage (nikah)
C) Khul' and manumission for payment
D) Hire (ijarah)

Key Takeaway
Writing and speech are equivalent in contracts; the council is when the message is received, but whether the half depends determines the rules on withdrawal and conditioning.
